\VersePair{18:20}{Forasmuch as evil is rewarded for good; for they have spoken words against my soul, and they have hidden the punishment they meant for me; remember that I stood before thy face, to speak good for them, to turn away thy wrath from them.}{18:20}{{\raggedright Should evil be recompensed for good? \poemline{2}{For they have dug a pit for my soul.}\poemline{1}{Remember how I stood before you to speak good for them,}\poemline{2}{to turn away your wrath from them.}}}
\VersePair{18:21}{Therefore do thou deliver their sons to famine, and gather them to the power of the sword: let their women be childless and widows; and let their men be cut off by death, and their young men fall by the sword in war.}{18:21}{{\raggedright Therefore deliver up their children to the famine, \poemline{2}{and give them over to the power of the sword.}\poemline{1}{Let their wives become childless and widows.}\poemline{2}{Let their men be killed}\poemline{2}{and their young men struck by the sword in battle.}}}
\VersePair{18:22}{Let there be a cry in their houses: thou shalt bring upon them robbers suddenly: for they have formed a plan to take me, and have hidden snares for me.}{18:22}{{\raggedright Let a cry be heard from their houses \poemline{2}{when you bring a troop suddenly on them;}\poemline{1}{for they have dug a pit to take me}\poemline{2}{and hidden snares for my feet.}}}
\VersePair{18:23}{And thou, Lord, knowest all their deadly counsel against me: account not their iniquities guiltless, and blot not out their sins from before thee: let their weakness come before thee; deal with them in the time of thy wrath.}{18:23}{{\raggedright Yet, Yahweh, you know all their counsel against me to kill me. \poemline{2}{Don’t forgive their iniquity.}\poemline{2}{Don’t blot out their sin from your sight,}\poemline{1}{Let them be overthrown before you.}\poemline{2}{Deal with them in the time of your anger.}}}
\end{paracol}
\ChapterHeading{19}
\begin{paracol}{2}
\VersePair{19:1}{Then said the Lord to me, Go and get an earthen bottle, the work of the potter, and thou shalt bring some of the elders of the people, and of the priests;}{19:1}{Thus said Yahweh, “Go, and buy a potter’s earthen container, and take some of the elders of the people and of the elders of the priests;}
\VersePair{19:2}{and thou shalt go forth to the burial-place of the sons of their children, which is at the entrance of the gate of Charsith; and do thou read there all these words which I shall speak to thee:}{19:2}{and go out to the valley of the son of Hinnom, which is by the entry of the gate Harsith, and proclaim there the words that I will tell you.}
\VersePair{19:3}{and thou shalt say to them, Hear ye the word of the Lord, ye kings of Juda, and men of Juda, and the dwellers in Jerusalem, and they that enter in by these gates; thus saith the Lord God of Israel; Behold, I will bring evil upon this place, so that the ears of every one that hears it shall tingle.}{19:3}{Say, ‘Hear Yahweh’s word, kings of Judah and inhabitants of Jerusalem: Yahweh of Armies, the God of Israel says, “Behold, I will bring evil on this place, which whoever hears, his ears will tingle.}
\VersePair{19:4}{Because they forsook me, and profaned this place, and burnt incense in it to strange gods, which they and their fathers knew not; and the kings of Juda have filled this place with innocent blood,}{19:4}{Because they have forsaken me, and have defiled this place, and have burned incense in it to other gods that they didn’t know — they, their fathers, and the kings of Judah — and have filled this place with the blood of innocents,}
\VersePair{19:5}{and built high places for Baal, to burn their children in the fire, which things I commanded not, neither did I design them in my heart:}{19:5}{and have built the high places of Baal to burn their children in the fire for burnt offerings to Baal, which I didn’t command, nor speak, which didn’t even enter into my mind.}
\VersePair{19:6}{Therefore, behold, the days come, saith the Lord, when this place shall no more be called, The fall and burial-place of the son of Ennom, but, The burial-place of slaughter.}{19:6}{Therefore, behold, the days come,” says Yahweh, “that this place will no more be called ‘Topheth ’, nor ‘The Valley of the son of Hinnom ’, but ‘The valley of Slaughter ’.}
\VersePair{19:7}{And I will destroy the counsel of Juda and the counsel of Jerusalem in this place; and I will cast them down with the sword before their enemies, and by the hands of them that seek their lives: and I will give their dead bodies for food to the birds of the sky and to the wild beasts of the earth.}{19:7}{“‘“I will make the counsel of Judah and Jerusalem void in this place. I will cause them to fall by the sword before their enemies, and by the hand of those who seek their life. I will give their dead bodies to be food for the birds of the sky and for the animals of the earth.}
\VersePair{19:8}{And I will bring this city to desolation and make it a hissing; every one that passes by it shall scowl, and hiss because of all her plague.}{19:8}{I will make this city an astonishment and a hissing. Everyone who passes by it will be astonished and hiss because of all its plagues.}
\VersePair{19:9}{And they shall eat the flesh of their sons, and the flesh of their daughters; and they shall eat every one the flesh of his neighbour in the blockade, and in the siege wherewith their enemies shall besiege them.}{19:9}{I will cause them to eat the flesh of their sons and the flesh of their daughters. They will each eat the flesh of his friend in the siege and in the distress with which their enemies, and those who seek their life, will distress them.”’}
\VersePair{19:10}{And thou shalt break the bottle in the sight of the men that go forth with thee,}{19:10}{“Then you shall break the container in the sight of the men who go with you,}
\VersePair{19:11}{and thou shalt say, Thus saith the Lord, Thus will I break in pieces this people, and this city, even as an earthen vessel is broken in pieces which cannot be mended again.}{19:11}{and shall tell them, ‘Yahweh of Armies says: “Even so I will break this people and this city as one breaks a potter’s vessel, that can’t be made whole again. They will bury in Topheth until there is no place to bury.}
\VersePair{19:12}{Thus will I do, saith the Lord, to this place, and to the inhabitants of it, that this city may be given up, as one that is falling to ruin.}{19:12}{This is what I will do to this place,” says Yahweh, “and to its inhabitants, even making this city as Topheth.}
\VersePair{19:13}{And the houses of Jerusalem, and the houses of the kings of Juda shall be as a ruinous place, because of their uncleannesses in all the houses, wherein they burnt incense upon their roofs to all the host of heaven, and poured drink-offerings to strange gods.}{19:13}{The houses of Jerusalem and the houses of the kings of Judah, which are defiled, will be as the place of Topheth, even all the houses on whose roofs they have burned incense to all the army of the sky and have poured out drink offerings to other gods.”’”}
\VersePair{19:14}{And Jeremias came from the place of the Fall, whither the Lord had sent him to prophesy; and he stood in the court of the Lord's house; and said to all the people, Thus saith the Lord;}{19:14}{Then Jeremiah came from Topheth, where Yahweh had sent him to prophesy, and he stood in the court of Yahweh’s house, and said to all the people:}
\VersePair{19:15}{Behold, I bring upon this city, and upon all the cities belonging to it, and upon the villages of it, all the evils which I have spoken against it, because they have hardened their neck, that they might not hearken to my commands.}{19:15}{“Yahweh of Armies, the God of Israel says, ‘Behold, I will bring on this city and on all its towns all the evil that I have pronounced against it, because they have made their neck stiff, that they may not hear my words.’”}
\end{paracol}
\ChapterHeading{20}
\begin{paracol}{2}
\VersePair{20:1}{Now Paschor the son of Emmer, the priest, who also had been appointed chief of the house of the Lord, heard Jeremias prophesying these words.}{20:1}{Now Pashhur, the son of Immer the priest, who was chief officer in Yahweh’s house, heard Jeremiah prophesying these things.}
\VersePair{20:2}{And he smote him, and cast him into the dungeon which was by the gate of the upper house that was set apart, which was by the house of the Lord.}{20:2}{Then Pashhur struck Jeremiah the prophet and put him in the stocks that were in the upper gate of Benjamin, which was in Yahweh’s house.}
\VersePair{20:3}{And Paschor brought Jeremias out of the dungeon: and Jeremias said to him, The Lord has not called thy name Paschor, but Exile.}{20:3}{On the next day, Pashhur released Jeremiah out of the stocks. Then Jeremiah said to him, “Yahweh has not called your name Pashhur, but Magormissabib. \footnote{20:3: “Magormissabib” means “surrounded by terror”}}
\VersePair{20:4}{For thus saith the Lord, Behold, I will give thee up to captivity with all thy friends: and they shall fall by the sword of their enemies, and thine eyes shall see it: and I will give thee and all Juda into the hands of the king of Babylon, and they shall carry them captives, and cut them in pieces with swords.}{20:4}{For Yahweh says, ‘Behold, I will make you a terror to yourself and to all your friends. They will fall by the sword of their enemies, and your eyes will see it. I will give all Judah into the hand of the king of Babylon, and he will carry them captive to Babylon, and will kill them with the sword.}
\VersePair{20:5}{And I will give all the strength of this city, and all the labours of it, and all the treasures of the king of Juda, into the hands of his enemies, and they shall bring them to Babylon.}{20:5}{Moreover I will give all the riches of this city, and all its gains, and all its precious things, yes, I will give all the treasures of the kings of Judah into the hand of their enemies. They will make them captives, take them, and carry them to Babylon.}
\VersePair{20:6}{And thou and all the dwellers in thine house shall go into captivity: and thou shalt die in Babylon, and there thou and all thy friends shall be buried, to whom thou hast prophesied lies.}{20:6}{You, Pashhur, and all who dwell in your house will go into captivity. You will come to Babylon, and there you will die, and there you will be buried, you, and all your friends, to whom you have prophesied falsely.’”}
\VersePair{20:7}{Thou hast deceived me, O Lord, and I have been deceived: thou hast been strong, and hast prevailed: I am become a laughing-stock, I am continually mocked every day.}{20:7}{{\raggedright Yahweh, you have persuaded me, and I was persuaded. \poemline{2}{You are stronger than I, and have prevailed.}\poemline{1}{I have become a laughingstock all day.}\poemline{2}{Everyone mocks me.}}}
\VersePair{20:8}{For I will laugh with my bitter speech, I will call upon rebellion and misery: for the word of the Lord is become a reproach to me and a mockery all my days.}{20:8}{{\raggedright For as often as I speak, I cry out; \poemline{2}{I cry, “Violence and destruction!”}\poemline{1}{because Yahweh’s word has been made a reproach to me,}\poemline{2}{and a derision, all day.}}}
\VersePair{20:9}{Then I said, I will by no means name the name of the Lord, and I will no more at all speak in his name. But it was as burning fire flaming in my bones, and I am utterly weakened on all sides, and cannot bear up.}{20:9}{{\raggedright If I say that I will not make mention of him, \poemline{2}{or speak any more in his name,}\poemline{1}{then there is in my heart as it were a burning fire shut up in my bones.}\poemline{2}{I am weary with holding it in.}\poemline{2}{I can’t.}}}
\VersePair{20:10}{For I have heard the reproach of many gathering round, saying, Conspire ye, and let us conspire together against him, even all his friends: watch his intentions, if perhaps he shall be deceived, and we shall prevail against him, and we shall be avenged on him.}{20:10}{{\raggedright For I have heard the defaming of many: \poemline{2}{“Terror on every side!}\poemline{2}{Denounce, and we will denounce him!”}\poemline{1}{say all my familiar friends,}\poemline{2}{those who watch for my fall.}\poemline{1}{“Perhaps he will be persuaded,}\poemline{2}{and we will prevail against him,}\poemline{2}{and we will take our revenge on him.”}}}
\VersePair{20:11}{But the Lord was with me as a mighty man of war: therefore they persecuted me, but could not perceive anything against me; they were greatly confounded, for they perceived not their disgrace, which shall never be forgotten.}{20:11}{{\raggedright But Yahweh is with me as an awesome mighty one. \poemline{2}{Therefore my persecutors will stumble,}\poemline{2}{and they won’t prevail.}\poemline{1}{They will be utterly disappointed}\poemline{2}{because they have not dealt wisely,}\poemline{2}{even with an everlasting dishonor which will never be forgotten.}}}
\VersePair{20:12}{O Lord, that provest just deeds, understanding the reins and hearts, let me see thy vengeance upon them: for to thee I have revealed my cause.}{20:12}{{\raggedright But Yahweh of Armies, who tests the righteous, \poemline{2}{who sees the heart and the mind,}\poemline{1}{let me see your vengeance on them,}\poemline{2}{for I have revealed my cause to you.}}}
\VersePair{20:13}{Sing ye to the Lord, sing praise to him: for he has rescued the soul of the poor from the hand of evil-doers.}{20:13}{{\raggedright Sing to Yahweh! \poemline{2}{Praise Yahweh,}\poemline{2}{for he has delivered the soul of the needy from the hand of evildoers.}}}
\VersePair{20:14}{Cursed be the day wherein I was born: the day wherein my mother brought me forth, let it not be blessed.}{20:14}{{\raggedright Cursed is the day in which I was born. \poemline{2}{Don’t let the day in which my mother bore me be blessed.}}}
\VersePair{20:15}{Cursed be the man who brought the glad tidings to my father, saying, A male child is born to thee.}{20:15}{{\raggedright Cursed is the man who brought news to my father, saying, \poemline{2}{“A boy is born to you,” making him very glad.}}}
\VersePair{20:16}{Let that man rejoice as the cities which the Lord overthrew in wrath, and repented not: let him hear crying in the morning, and loud lamentation at noon;}{20:16}{{\raggedright Let that man be as the cities which Yahweh overthrew, \poemline{2}{and didn’t repent.}\poemline{1}{Let him hear a cry in the morning,}\poemline{2}{and shouting at noontime,}}}
\VersePair{20:17}{because he slew me not in the womb, and my mother became not my tomb, and her womb always great with me.}{20:17}{{\raggedright because he didn’t kill me from the womb. \poemline{2}{So my mother would have been my grave,}\poemline{2}{and her womb always great.}}}
\VersePair{20:18}{Why is it that I came forth of the womb to see troubles and distresses, and my days are spent in shame?}{20:18}{{\raggedright Why did I come out of the womb to see labor and sorrow, \poemline{2}{that my days should be consumed with shame?}}}
\end{paracol}
\ChapterHeading{21}
\begin{paracol}{2}
\VersePair{21:1}{The Word that came from the Lord to Jeremias, when King Sedekias sent to him Paschor the Son of Melchias, and Sophonias Son of Basæas, the Priest, saying,}{21:1}{The word which came to Jeremiah from Yahweh, when King Zedekiah sent to him Pashhur the son of Malchijah, and Zephaniah the son of Maaseiah, the priest, saying,}
\VersePair{21:2}{Enquire of the Lord for us; for the king of Babylon has risen up against us; if the Lord will do according to all his wonderful works, and the king shall depart from us.}{21:2}{“Please inquire of Yahweh for us; for Nebuchadnezzar king of Babylon makes war against us. Perhaps Yahweh will deal with us according to all his wondrous works, that he may withdraw from us.”}
\VersePair{21:3}{And Jeremias said to them, Thus shall ye say to Sedekias king of Juda,}{21:3}{Then Jeremiah said to them, “Tell Zedekiah:}
\VersePair{21:4}{Thus saith the Lord; Behold, I will turn back the weapons of war wherewith ye fight against the Chaldeans that have besieged you from outside the wall, and I will gather them into the midst of this city.}{21:4}{‘Yahweh, the God of Israel says, “Behold, I will turn back the weapons of war that are in your hands, with which you fight against the king of Babylon, and against the Chaldeans who besiege you outside the walls; and I will gather them into the middle of this city.}
\VersePair{21:5}{And I will fight against you with an outstretched hand and with a strong arm, with wrath and great anger.}{21:5}{I myself will fight against you with an outstretched hand and with a strong arm, even in anger, in wrath, and in great indignation.}
\VersePair{21:6}{And I will smite all the dwellers in this city, both men and cattle, with grievous pestilence: and they shall die.}{21:6}{I will strike the inhabitants of this city, both man and animal. They will die of a great pestilence.}
\VersePair{21:7}{And after this, thus saith the Lord; I will give Sedekias king of Juda, and his servants, and the people that is left in this city from the pestilence, and from the famine, and from the sword, into the hands of their enemies, that seek their lives: and they shall cut them in pieces with the edge of the sword: I will not spare them, and I will not have compassion upon them.}{21:7}{Afterward,” says Yahweh, “I will deliver Zedekiah king of Judah, his servants, and the people, even those who are left in this city from the pestilence, from the sword, and from the famine, into the hand of Nebuchadnezzar king of Babylon, and into the hand of their enemies, and into the hand of those who seek their life. He will strike them with the edge of the sword. He will not spare them, have pity, or have mercy.”’}
\VersePair{21:8}{And thou shalt say to this people, Thus saith the Lord; Behold, I have set before you the way of life, and the way of death.}{21:8}{“You shall say to this people, ‘Yahweh says: “Behold, I set before you the way of life and the way of death.}
\VersePair{21:9}{He that remains in this city shall die by the sword, and by famine: but he that goes forth to advance to the Chaldeans that have besieged you, shall live, and his life shall be to him for a spoil, and he shall live.}{21:9}{He who remains in this city will die by the sword, by the famine, and by the pestilence, but he who goes out and passes over to the Chaldeans who besiege you, he will live, and he will escape with his life.}
\VersePair{21:10}{For I have set my face against this city for evil, and not for good: it shall be delivered into the hands of the king of Babylon, and he shall consume it with fire.}{21:10}{For I have set my face on this city for evil, and not for good,” says Yahweh. “It will be given into the hand of the king of Babylon, and he will burn it with fire.”’}
\VersePair{21:11}{O house of the king of Juda, hear ye the word of the Lord.}{21:11}{“Concerning the house of the king of Judah, hear Yahweh’s word:}
\VersePair{21:12}{O house of David, thus saith the Lord; Judge judgment in the morning, and act rightly, and rescue the spoiled one from the hand of him that wrongs him, lest mine anger be kindled like fire, and it burn, and there be none to quench it.}{21:12}{{\raggedright House of David, Yahweh says, \poemline{1}{‘Execute justice in the morning,}\poemline{2}{and deliver him who is robbed out of the hand of the oppressor,}\poemline{1}{lest my wrath go out like fire,}\poemline{2}{and burn so that no one can quench it,}\poemline{2}{because of the evil of your doings.}}}
\VersePair{21:13}{Behold, I am against thee that dwellest in the valley of Sor; in the plain country, even against them that say, Who shall alarm us? or who shall enter into our habitation?}{21:13}{{\raggedright Behold, I am against you, O inhabitant of the valley, \poemline{2}{and of the rock of the plain,’ says Yahweh.}\poemline{1}{‘You that say, “Who would come down against us?”}\poemline{2}{or, “Who would enter into our homes?”}}}
\VersePair{21:14}{And I will kindle a fire in the forest thereof, and it shall devour all things round about it.}{21:14}{{\raggedright I will punish you according to the fruit of your doings,’ says Yahweh; \poemline{2}{‘and I will kindle a fire in her forest,}\poemline{2}{and it will devour all that is around her.’”}}}
\end{paracol}
\ChapterHeading{22}
\begin{paracol}{2}
\VersePair{22:1}{Thus saith the Lord; Go thou, and go down to the house of the king of Juda, and thou shalt speak there this word,}{22:1}{Yahweh said, “Go down to the house of the king of Judah, and speak this word there:}
\VersePair{22:2}{and thou shalt say, Hear the word of the Lord, O king of Juda, that sittest on the throne of David, thou, and thy house, and thy people, and they that go in at these gates:}{22:2}{‘Hear Yahweh’s word, king of Judah, who sits on David’s throne — you, your servants, and your people who enter in by these gates.}
\VersePair{22:3}{thus saith the Lord; Execute ye judgment and justice, and rescue the spoiled out of the hand of him that wrongs him: and oppress not the stranger, and orphan, and widow, and sin not, and shed no innocent blood in this place.}{22:3}{Yahweh says: “Execute justice and righteousness, and deliver him who is robbed out of the hand of the oppressor. Do no wrong. Do no violence to the foreigner, the fatherless, or the widow. Don’t shed innocent blood in this place.}
\VersePair{22:4}{For if ye will indeed perform this word, then shall there enter in by the gates of this house kings sitting upon the throne of David, and riding on chariots and horses, they, and their servants, and their people.}{22:4}{For if you do this thing indeed, then kings sitting on David’s throne will enter in by the gates of this house, riding in chariots and on horses — they, their servants, and their people.}
\VersePair{22:5}{But if ye will not perform these words, by myself have I sworn, saith the Lord, that this house shall be brought to desolation.}{22:5}{But if you will not hear these words, I swear by myself,” says Yahweh, “that this house will become a desolation.”’”}
\VersePair{22:6}{For thus saith the Lord concerning the house of the king of Juda; Thou art Galaad to me, and the head of Libanus: yet surely I will make thee a desert, even cities that shall not be inhabited:}{22:6}{{\raggedright For Yahweh says concerning the house of the king of Judah: \poemline{1}{“You are Gilead to me,}\poemline{2}{the head of Lebanon.}\poemline{1}{Yet surely I will make you a wilderness,}\poemline{2}{cities which are not inhabited.}}}
\VersePair{22:7}{and I will bring upon thee a destroying man, and his axe: and they shall cut down thy choice cedars, and cast them into the fire.}{22:7}{{\raggedright I will prepare destroyers against you, \poemline{2}{everyone with his weapons,}\poemline{1}{and they will cut down your choice cedars,}\poemline{2}{and cast them into the fire.}}}
\VersePair{22:8}{And nations shall pass through this city, and each shall say to his neighbour, Why has the Lord done thus to this great city?}{22:8}{“Many nations will pass by this city, and they will each ask his neighbor, ‘Why has Yahweh done this to this great city?’}
\VersePair{22:9}{And they shall say, Because they forsook the covenant of the Lord their God, and worshipped strange gods, and served them.}{22:9}{Then they will answer, ‘Because they abandoned the covenant of Yahweh their God, worshiped other gods, and served them.’”}
\VersePair{22:10}{Weep not for the dead, nor lament for him: weep bitterly for him that goes away: for he shall return no more, nor see his native land.}{22:10}{{\raggedright Don’t weep for the dead. \poemline{2}{Don’t bemoan him;}\poemline{1}{but weep bitterly for him who goes away,}\poemline{2}{for he will return no more,}\poemline{2}{and not see his native country.}}}
\VersePair{22:11}{For thus saith the Lord concerning Sellem the son of Josias, who reigns in the place of Josias his father, who has gone forth out of this place; He shall not return thither any more:}{22:11}{For Yahweh says touching Shallum the son of Josiah, king of Judah, who reigned instead of Josiah his father, and who went out of this place: “He won’t return there any more.}
\VersePair{22:12}{but in that place whither I have carried him captive, there shall he die, and shall see this land no more.}{22:12}{But he will die in the place where they have led him captive. He will see this land no more.”}
\VersePair{22:13}{He that builds his house not with justice, and his upper chambers not with judgment, who works by means of his neighbour for nothing, and will by no means give him his reward.}{22:13}{{\raggedright “Woe to him who builds his house by unrighteousness, \poemline{2}{and his rooms by injustice;}\poemline{1}{who uses his neighbor’s service without wages,}\poemline{2}{and doesn’t give him his hire;}}}
\VersePair{22:14}{Thou hast built for thyself a well-proportioned house, airy chambers, fitted with windows, and wainscoted with cedar, and painted with vermilion.}{22:14}{{\raggedright who says, ‘I will build myself a wide house and spacious rooms,’ \poemline{2}{and cuts out windows for himself,}\poemline{1}{with a cedar ceiling,}\poemline{2}{and painted with red.}}}
\VersePair{22:15}{Shalt thou reign, because thou art provoked with thy father Achaz? they shall not eat, and they shall not drink: it is better for thee to execute judgment and justice.}{22:15}{{\raggedright “Should you reign because you strive to excel in cedar? \poemline{2}{Didn’t your father eat and drink,}\poemline{2}{and do justice and righteousness?}\poemline{2}{Then it was well with him.}}}
\VersePair{22:16}{They understood not, they judged not the cause of the afflicted, nor the cause of the poor: is not this thy not knowing me? saith the Lord.}{22:16}{{\raggedright He judged the cause of the poor and needy; \poemline{2}{so then it was well.}\poemline{1}{Wasn’t this to know me?”}\poemline{2}{says Yahweh.}}}
\VersePair{22:17}{Behold, thine eyes are not good, nor thine heart, but they go after thy covetousness, and after the innocent blood to shed it, and after acts of injustice and slaughter, to commit them.}{22:17}{{\raggedright But your eyes and your heart are only for your covetousness, \poemline{2}{for shedding innocent blood,}\poemline{2}{for oppression, and for doing violence.”}}}
\VersePair{22:18}{Therefore thus saith the Lord concerning Joakim son of Josias, king of Juda, even concerning this man; they shall not bewail him, saying, Ah brother! neither shall they at all weep for him, saying, Alas Lord.}{22:18}{{\raggedright Therefore Yahweh says concerning Jehoiakim the son of Josiah, king of Judah: \poemline{1}{“They won’t lament for him,}\poemline{2}{saying, ‘Ah my brother!’ or, ‘Ah sister!’}\poemline{1}{They won’t lament for him,}\poemline{2}{saying ‘Ah lord!’ or, ‘Ah his glory!’}}}
\VersePair{22:19}{He shall be buried with the burial of an ass; he shall be dragged roughly along and cast outside the gate of Jerusalem.}{22:19}{{\raggedright He will be buried with the burial of a donkey, \poemline{2}{drawn and cast out beyond the gates of Jerusalem.”}}}
\VersePair{22:20}{Go up to Libanus, and cry; and utter thy voice to Basan, and cry aloud to the extremity of the sea: for all thy lovers are destroyed.}{22:20}{{\raggedright “Go up to Lebanon, and cry out. \poemline{2}{Lift up your voice in Bashan,}\poemline{1}{and cry from Abarim;}\poemline{2}{for all your lovers have been destroyed.}}}
\VersePair{22:21}{I spoke to thee on occasion of thy trespass, but thou saidst, I will not hearken. This has been thy way from thy youth, thou hast not hearkened to my voice.}{22:21}{{\raggedright I spoke to you in your prosperity, \poemline{2}{but you said, ‘I will not listen.’}\poemline{1}{This has been your way from your youth,}\poemline{2}{that you didn’t obey my voice.}}}
\VersePair{22:22}{The wind shall tend all thy shepherds, and thy lovers shall go into captivity; for then shalt thou be ashamed and disgraced because of all thy lovers.}{22:22}{{\raggedright The wind will feed all your shepherds, \poemline{2}{and your lovers will go into captivity.}\poemline{1}{Surely then you will be ashamed}\poemline{2}{and confounded for all your wickedness.}}}
\VersePair{22:23}{O thou that dwellest in Libanus, making thy nest in the cedars, thou shalt groan heavily, when pangs as of a travailing woman are come upon thee.}{22:23}{{\raggedright Inhabitant of Lebanon, \poemline{2}{who makes your nest in the cedars,}\poemline{1}{how greatly to be pitied you will be when pangs come on you,}\poemline{2}{the pain as of a woman in travail!}}}
\VersePair{22:24}{As I live, saith the Lord, though Jechonias son of Joakim king of Juda were indeed the seal upon my right hand, thence would I pluck thee;}{22:24}{“As I live,” says Yahweh, “though Coniah the son of Jehoiakim king of Judah were the signet on my right hand, I would still pluck you from there.}
\VersePair{22:25}{and I will deliver thee into the hands of them that seek thy life, before whom thou art afraid, into the hands of the Chaldeans.}{22:25}{I would give you into the hand of those who seek your life, and into the hand of them of whom you are afraid, even into the hand of Nebuchadnezzar king of Babylon, and into the hand of the Chaldeans.}
\VersePair{22:26}{And I will cast forth thee, and thy mother that bore thee, into a land where thou wast not born; and there ye shall die.}{22:26}{I will cast you out with your mother who bore you into another country, where you were not born; and there you will die.}
\VersePair{22:27}{But they shall by no means return to the land which they long for in their souls.}{22:27}{But to the land to which their soul longs to return, there they will not return.”}
\VersePair{22:28}{Jechonias is dishonoured as a good-for-nothing vessel; for he is thrown out and cast forth into a land which he knew not.}{22:28}{{\raggedright Is this man Coniah a despised broken vessel? \poemline{2}{Is he a vessel in which no one delights?}\poemline{1}{Why are they cast out, he and his offspring,}\poemline{2}{and cast into a land which they don’t know?}}}
\VersePair{22:29}{Land, land, hear the word of the Lord.}{22:29}{{\raggedright O earth, earth, earth, \poemline{2}{hear Yahweh’s word!}}}
\VersePair{22:30}{Write ye this man an outcast: for there shall none of his seed at all grow up to sit on the throne of David, or as a prince yet in Juda.}{22:30}{{\raggedright Yahweh says, \poemline{2}{“Record this man as childless,}\poemline{2}{a man who will not prosper in his days;}\poemline{1}{for no more will a man of his offspring prosper,}\poemline{2}{sitting on David’s throne}\poemline{2}{and ruling in Judah.”}}}
\end{paracol}
\ChapterHeading{23}
\begin{paracol}{2}
\VersePair{23:1}{Woe to the shepherds that destroy and scatter the sheep of their pasture!}{23:1}{“Woe to the shepherds who destroy and scatter the sheep of my pasture!” says Yahweh.}
\VersePair{23:2}{Therefore thus saith the Lord against them that tend my people; Ye have scattered my sheep, and driven them out, and ye have not visited them: behold, I will take vengeance upon you according to your evil practices.}{23:2}{Therefore Yahweh, the God of Israel, says against the shepherds who feed my people: “You have scattered my flock, driven them away, and have not visited them. Behold, I will visit on you the evil of your doings,” says Yahweh.}
\VersePair{23:3}{And I will gather in the remnant of my people in every land, whither I have driven them out, and will set them in their pasture; and they shall increase and be multiplied.}{23:3}{“I will gather the remnant of my flock out of all the countries where I have driven them, and will bring them again to their folds; and they will be fruitful and multiply.}
\VersePair{23:4}{And I will raise up shepherds to them, who shall feed them: and they shall fear no more, nor be alarmed, saith the Lord.}{23:4}{I will set up shepherds over them who will feed them. They will no longer be afraid or dismayed, neither will any be lacking,” says Yahweh.}
\VersePair{23:5}{Behold, the days come, saith the Lord, when I will raise up to David a righteous branch, and a king shall reign and understand, and shall execute judgment and righteousness on the earth.}{23:5}{{\raggedright “Behold, the days come,” says Yahweh, \poemline{2}{“that I will raise to David a righteous Branch;}\poemline{1}{and he will reign as king and deal wisely,}\poemline{2}{and will execute justice and righteousness in the land.}}}
\VersePair{23:6}{In his days both Juda shall be saved, and Israel shall dwell securely: and this is his name, which the Lord shall call him, Josedec among the prophets.}{23:6}{{\raggedright In his days Judah will be saved, \poemline{2}{and Israel will dwell safely.}\poemline{1}{This is his name by which he will be called:}\poemline{2}{Yahweh our righteousness.}}}
\VersePair{23:9}{My heart is broken within me; all my bones are shaken: I am become as a broken-down man, and as a man overcome with wine, because of the Lord, and because of the excellence of his glory.}{23:9}{{\raggedright Concerning the prophets: \poemline{1}{My heart within me is broken.}\poemline{2}{All my bones shake.}\poemline{1}{I am like a drunken man,}\poemline{2}{and like a man whom wine has overcome,}\poemline{1}{because of Yahweh,}\poemline{2}{and because of his holy words.}}}
\VersePair{23:10}{For because of these things the land mourns; the pastures of the wilderness are dried up; and their course is become evil, and so also their strength.}{23:10}{{\raggedright “For the land is full of adulterers; \poemline{2}{for because of the curse the land mourns.}\poemline{1}{The pastures of the wilderness have dried up.}\poemline{2}{Their course is evil,}\poemline{2}{and their might is not right;}}}
\VersePair{23:11}{For priest and prophet are defiled; and I have seen their iniquities in my house.}{23:11}{{\raggedright for both prophet and priest are profane. \poemline{2}{Yes, in my house I have found their wickedness,” says Yahweh.}}}
\VersePair{23:12}{Therefore let their way be to them slippery and dark: and they shall be tripped up and fall in it: for I will bring evils upon them, in the year of their visitation.}{23:12}{{\raggedright Therefore their way will be to them as slippery places in the darkness. \poemline{2}{They will be driven on,}\poemline{2}{and fall therein;}\poemline{1}{for I will bring evil on them,}\poemline{2}{even the year of their visitation,” says Yahweh.}}}
\VersePair{23:13}{And in the prophets of Samaria I have seen lawless deeds; they prophesied by Baal, and led my people Israel astray.}{23:13}{{\raggedright “I have seen folly in the prophets of Samaria. \poemline{2}{They prophesied by Baal,}\poemline{2}{and caused my people Israel to err.}}}
\VersePair{23:14}{Also in the prophets of Jerusalem I have seen horrible things: as they committed adultery, and walked in lies, and strengthened the hands of many, that they should not return each from his evil way: they are all become to me as Sodoma, and the inhabitants thereof as Gomorrha.}{23:14}{{\raggedright In the prophets of Jerusalem I have also seen a horrible thing: \poemline{2}{they commit adultery and walk in lies.}\poemline{1}{They strengthen the hands of evildoers,}\poemline{2}{so that no one returns from his wickedness.}\poemline{1}{They have all become to me as Sodom,}\poemline{2}{and its inhabitants as Gomorrah.”}}}
\VersePair{23:15}{Therefore thus saith the Lord; Behold, I will feed them with pain, and give them bitter water to drink: for from the prophets of Jerusalem has defilement gone forth into all the land.}{23:15}{{\raggedright Therefore Yahweh of Armies says concerning the prophets: \poemline{1}{“Behold, I will feed them with wormwood,}\poemline{2}{and make them drink poisoned water;}\poemline{2}{for from the prophets of Jerusalem ungodliness has gone out into all the land.”}}}
\VersePair{23:16}{Thus saith the Lord Almighty, Hearken not to the words of the prophets: for they frame a vain vision for themselves; they speak from their own heart, and not from the mouth of the Lord.}{23:16}{{\raggedright Yahweh of Armies says, \poemline{1}{“Don’t listen to the words of the prophets who prophesy to you.}\poemline{2}{They teach you vanity.}\poemline{2}{They speak a vision of their own heart,}\poemline{2}{and not out of the mouth of Yahweh.}}}
\VersePair{23:17}{They say to them that reject the word of the Lord, There shall be peace to you; and to all that walk after their own lusts, and to every one that walks in the error of his heart, they have said, No evil shall come upon thee.}{23:17}{{\raggedright They say continually to those who despise me, \poemline{2}{‘Yahweh has said, “You will have peace;”’}\poemline{1}{and to everyone who walks in the stubbornness of his own heart they say,}\poemline{2}{‘No evil will come on you.’}}}
\VersePair{23:18}{For who has stood in the counsel of the Lord, and seen his word? who has hearkened, and heard?}{23:18}{{\raggedright For who has stood in the council of Yahweh, \poemline{2}{that he should perceive and hear his word?}\poemline{2}{Who has listened to my word, and heard it?}}}
\VersePair{23:19}{Behold, there is an earthquake from the Lord, and anger proceeds to a convulsion, it shall come violently upon the ungodly.}{23:19}{{\raggedright Behold, Yahweh’s storm, his wrath, has gone out. \poemline{2}{Yes, a whirling storm!}\poemline{2}{It will burst on the head of the wicked.}}}
\VersePair{23:20}{And the Lord's wrath shall return no more, until he have accomplished it, and until he have established it, according to the purpose of his heart: at the end of the days they shall understand it.}{23:20}{{\raggedright Yahweh’s anger will not return until he has executed \poemline{2}{and performed the intents of his heart.}\poemline{2}{In the latter days, you will understand it perfectly.}}}
\VersePair{23:21}{I sent not the prophets, yet they ran: neither spoke I to them, yet they prophesied.}{23:21}{{\raggedright I didn’t send these prophets, yet they ran. \poemline{2}{I didn’t speak to them, yet they prophesied.}}}
\VersePair{23:22}{But if they had stood in my counsel, and if they had hearkened to my words, then would they have turned my people from their evil practices.}{23:22}{{\raggedright But if they had stood in my council, \poemline{2}{then they would have caused my people to hear my words,}\poemline{1}{and would have turned them from their evil way,}\poemline{2}{and from the evil of their doings.}}}
\VersePair{23:23}{I am a God nigh at hand, saith the Lord, and not a God afar off.}{23:23}{{\raggedright “Am I a God at hand,” says Yahweh, \poemline{2}{“and not a God afar off?}}}
\VersePair{23:24}{Shall any one hide himself in secret places, and I not see him? Do I not fill heaven and earth? saith the Lord.}{23:24}{{\raggedright Can anyone hide himself in secret places \poemline{2}{so that I can’t see him?” says Yahweh.}\poemline{2}{“Don’t I fill heaven and earth?” says Yahweh.}}}
\VersePair{23:25}{I have heard what the prophets say, what they prophesy in my name, saying falsely, I have seen a night vision.}{23:25}{“I have heard what the prophets have said, who prophesy lies in my name, saying, ‘I had a dream! I had a dream!’}
\VersePair{23:26}{How long shall these things be in the heart of the prophets that prophesy lies, when they prophesy the purposes of their own heart?}{23:26}{How long will this be in the heart of the prophets who prophesy lies, even the prophets of the deceit of their own heart?}
\VersePair{23:27}{who devise that men may forget my law by their dreams, which they have told every one to his neighbour, as their fathers forgot my name in the worship of Baal.}{23:27}{They intend to cause my people to forget my name by their dreams which they each tell his neighbor, as their fathers forgot my name because of Baal.}
\VersePair{23:28}{The prophet who has a dream, let him tell his dream; and he in whom is my word spoken to him, let him tell my word truly: what is the chaff to the corn? so are my words, saith the Lord.}{23:28}{The prophet who has a dream, let him tell a dream; and he who has my word, let him speak my word faithfully. What is the straw to the wheat?” says Yahweh.}
\VersePair{23:29}{Behold, are not my words as fire? saith the Lord; and as an axe cutting the rock?}{23:29}{“Isn’t my word like fire?” says Yahweh; “and like a hammer that breaks the rock in pieces?}
\VersePair{23:30}{Behold, I am therefore against the prophets, saith the Lord God, that steal my words every one from his neighbour.}{23:30}{“Therefore behold, I am against the prophets,” says Yahweh, “who each steal my words from his neighbor.}
\VersePair{23:31}{Behold, I am against the prophets that put forth prophecies of mere words, and slumber their sleep.}{23:31}{Behold, I am against the prophets,” says Yahweh, “who use their tongues, and say, ‘He says.’}
\VersePair{23:32}{Therefore, behold, I am against the prophets that prophesy false dreams, and have not told them truly, and have caused my people to err by their lies, and by their errors; yet I sent them not, and commanded them not; therefore, they shall not profit this people at all.}{23:32}{Behold, I am against those who prophesy lying dreams,” says Yahweh, “who tell them, and cause my people to err by their lies, and by their vain boasting; yet I didn’t send them or command them. They don’t profit this people at all,” says Yahweh.}
\VersePair{23:33}{And if this people, or the priest, or the prophet, should ask, What is the burden of the Lord? then thou shalt say to them, Ye are the burden, and I will dash you down, saith the Lord.}{23:33}{“When this people, or the prophet, or a priest, asks you, saying, ‘What is the message from Yahweh?’ Then you shall tell them, ‘“What message? I will cast you off,” says Yahweh.’}
\VersePair{23:34}{As for the prophet, and the priests, and the people, who shall say, The burden of the Lord, I will even take vengeance on that man, and on his house.}{23:34}{As for the prophet, the priest, and the people, who say, ‘The message from Yahweh,’ I will even punish that man and his household.}
\VersePair{23:35}{Thus shall ye say every one to his neighbour, and every one to his brother, What has the Lord answered? and, what has the Lord said?}{23:35}{You will say everyone to his neighbor, and everyone to his brother, ‘What has Yahweh answered?’ and, ‘What has Yahweh said?’}
\VersePair{23:36}{And do ye name no more the burden of the Lord; for his own word shall be a man's burden.}{23:36}{You will mention the message from Yahweh no more, for every man’s own word has become his message; for you have perverted the words of the living God, of Yahweh of Armies, our God.}
\VersePair{23:37}{But wherefore, say ye, has the Lord our God spoken?}{23:37}{You will say to the prophet, ‘What has Yahweh answered you?’ and, ‘What has Yahweh spoken?’}
\VersePair{23:38}{Therefore thus saith the Lord our God; Because ye have spoken this word, The burden of the Lord, and I sent to you, saying, Ye shall not say, The burden of the Lord;}{23:38}{Although you say, ‘The message from Yahweh,’ therefore Yahweh says: ‘Because you say this word, “The message from Yahweh,” and I have sent to you, telling you not to say, “The message from Yahweh,”}
\VersePair{23:39}{therefore, behold, I will seize, and dash down you and the city which I gave to you and your fathers.}{23:39}{therefore behold, I will utterly forget you, and I will cast you off with the city that I gave to you and to your fathers, away from my presence.}
\VersePair{23:40}{And I will bring upon you an everlasting reproach, and everlasting disgrace, which shall not be forgotten.}{23:40}{I will bring an everlasting reproach on you, and a perpetual shame, which will not be forgotten.’”}
\VersePair{23:40a}{Therefore, behold, the days come, saith the Lord, when they shall no more say, The Lord lives, who brought up the house of Israel out of the land of Egypt;}{23:40a}{}
\VersePair{23:40b}{but The Lord lives, who has gathered the whole seed of Israel from the north land, and from all the countries whither he had driven them out, and has restored them into their own land.}{23:40b}{}
\end{paracol}
\ChapterHeading{24}
\begin{paracol}{2}
\VersePair{24:1}{The Lord shewed me two baskets of figs, lying in front of the temple of the Lord, after Nabuchodonosor king of Babylon had carried captive Jechonias son of Joakim king of Juda, and the princes, and the artificers, and the prisoners, and the rich men out of Jerusalem, and had brought them to Babylon.}{24:1}{Yahweh showed me, and behold, two baskets of figs were set before Yahweh’s temple, after Nebuchadnezzar king of Babylon had carried away captive Jeconiah the son of Jehoiakim, king of Judah, and the princes of Judah, with the craftsmen and smiths, from Jerusalem, and had brought them to Babylon.}
\VersePair{24:2}{The one basket was full of very good figs, as the early figs; and the other basket was full of very bad figs, which could not be eaten, for their badness.}{24:2}{One basket had very good figs, like the figs that are first-ripe; and the other basket had very bad figs, which could not be eaten, they were so bad.}
\VersePair{24:3}{And the Lord said to me, What seest thou, Jeremias? and I said, Figs; the good figs, very good; and the bad, very bad, which cannot be eaten, for their badness.}{24:3}{Then Yahweh asked me, “What do you see, Jeremiah?” I said, “Figs. The good figs are very good, and the bad are very bad, so bad that they can’t be eaten.”}
\VersePair{24:4}{And the word of the Lord came to me, saying,}{24:4}{Yahweh’s word came to me, saying,}
\VersePair{24:5}{Thus saith the Lord, the God of Israel; As these good figs, so will I acknowledge the Jews that have been carried away captive, whom I have sent forth out of this place into the land of the Chaldeans for good.}{24:5}{“Yahweh, the God of Israel says: ‘Like these good figs, so I will regard the captives of Judah, whom I have sent out of this place into the land of the Chaldeans, as good.}
\VersePair{24:6}{And I will fix mine eyes upon them for good, and I will restore them into this land for good: and I will build them up, and not pull them down; and I will plant them, and not pluck them up.}{24:6}{For I will set my eyes on them for good, and I will bring them again to this land. I will build them, and not pull them down. I will plant them, and not pluck them up.}
\VersePair{24:7}{And I will give them a heart to know me, that I am the Lord: and they shall be to me a people, and I will be to them a God: for they shall turn to me with all their heart.}{24:7}{I will give them a heart to know me, that I am Yahweh. They will be my people, and I will be their God; for they will return to me with their whole heart.}
\VersePair{24:8}{And as the bad figs, which cannot be eaten, for their badness; thus saith the Lord, So will I deliver Sedekias king of Juda, and his nobles, and the remnant of Jerusalem, them that are left in this land, and the dwellers in Egypt.}{24:8}{“‘As the bad figs, which can’t be eaten, they are so bad,’ surely Yahweh says, ‘So I will give up Zedekiah the king of Judah, and his princes, and the remnant of Jerusalem who remain in this land, and those who dwell in the land of Egypt.}
\VersePair{24:9}{And I will cause them to be dispersed into all the kingdoms of the earth, and they shall be for a reproach, and a proverb, and an object of hatred, and a curse, in every place whither I have driven them out.}{24:9}{I will even give them up to be tossed back and forth among all the kingdoms of the earth for evil, to be a reproach and a proverb, a taunt and a curse, in all places where I will drive them.}
\VersePair{24:10}{And I will send against them famine, and pestilence, and the sword, until they are consumed from off the land which I gave them.}{24:10}{I will send the sword, the famine, and the pestilence among them, until they are consumed from off the land that I gave to them and to their fathers.’”}
\end{paracol}
\ChapterHeading{25}
\begin{paracol}{2}
\VersePair{25:1}{The Word that came to Jeremias concerning all the people of Juda in the fourth year of Joakim, son of Josias, king of Juda;}{25:1}{The word that came to Jeremiah concerning all the people of Judah, in the fourth year of Jehoiakim the son of Josiah, king of Judah ( this was the first year of Nebuchadnezzar king of Babylon),}
\VersePair{25:2}{which he spoke to all the people of Juda, and to the inhabitants of Jerusalem, saying,}{25:2}{which Jeremiah the prophet spoke to all the people of Judah, and to all the inhabitants of Jerusalem:}
\VersePair{25:3}{In the thirteenth year of Josias, son of Amos, king of Juda, even until this day for three and twenty years, I have both spoken to you, rising early and speaking,}{25:3}{From the thirteenth year of Josiah the son of Amon, king of Judah, even to this day, these twenty-three years, Yahweh’s word has come to me, and I have spoken to you, rising up early and speaking; but you have not listened.}
\VersePair{25:4}{and I sent to you my servants the prophets, sending them early; (but ye hearkened not, and listened not with your ears;) saying,}{25:4}{Yahweh has sent to you all his servants the prophets, rising up early and sending them ( but you have not listened or inclined your ear to hear ),}
\VersePair{25:5}{Turn ye every one from his evil way, and from your evil practices, and ye shall dwell in the land which I gave to you and your fathers, of old and for ever.}{25:5}{saying, “Return now everyone from his evil way, and from the evil of your doings, and dwell in the land that Yahweh has given to you and to your fathers, from of old and even forever more.}
\VersePair{25:6}{Go ye not after strange gods, to serve them, and to worship them, that ye provoke me not by the works of your hands, to do you hurt.}{25:6}{Don’t go after other gods to serve them or worship them, and don’t provoke me to anger with the work of your hands; then I will do you no harm.”}
\VersePair{25:7}{But ye hearkened not to me.}{25:7}{“Yet you have not listened to me,” says Yahweh, “that you may provoke me to anger with the work of your hands to your own hurt.”}
\VersePair{25:8}{Therefore thus saith the Lord; Since ye believed not my words,}{25:8}{Therefore Yahweh of Armies says: “Because you have not heard my words,}
\VersePair{25:9}{behold, I will send and take a family from the north, and will bring them against this land, and against the inhabitants of it, and against all the nations round about it, and I will make them utterly waste, and make them a desolation, and a hissing, and an everlasting reproach.}{25:9}{behold, I will send and take all the families of the north,” says Yahweh, “and I will send to Nebuchadnezzar the king of Babylon, my servant, and will bring them against this land, and against its inhabitants, and against all these nations around. I will utterly destroy them, and make them an astonishment, and a hissing, and perpetual desolations.}
\VersePair{25:10}{And I will destroy from among them the voice of joy, and the voice of gladness, the voice of the bridegroom, and the voice of the bride, the scent of ointment, and the light of a candle.}{25:10}{Moreover I will take from them the voice of mirth and the voice of gladness, the voice of the bridegroom and the voice of the bride, the sound of the millstones, and the light of the lamp.}
\VersePair{25:11}{And all the land shall be a desolation; and they shall serve among the Gentiles seventy years.}{25:11}{This whole land will be a desolation, and an astonishment; and these nations will serve the king of Babylon seventy years.}
\VersePair{25:12}{And when the seventy years are fulfilled, I will take vengeance on that nation, and will make them a perpetual desolation.}{25:12}{“It will happen, when seventy years are accomplished, that I will punish the king of Babylon and that nation,” says Yahweh, “for their iniquity. I will make the land of the Chaldeans desolate forever.}
\VersePair{25:13}{And I will bring upon that land all my words which I have spoken against it, even all things that are written in this book.}{25:13}{I will bring on that land all my words which I have pronounced against it, even all that is written in this book, which Jeremiah has prophesied against all the nations.}
\VersePair{25:14}{The Prophecies of Jeremias against the Nations of Ælam.}{49:34}{Yahweh’s word that came to Jeremiah the prophet concerning Elam, in the beginning of the reign of Zedekiah king of Judah, saying,}
\VersePair{25:15}{Thus saith the Lord, The bow of Ælam is broken, even the chief of their power.}{49:35}{{\raggedright “Yahweh of Armies says: \poemline{1}{‘Behold, I will break the bow of Elam,}\poemline{2}{the chief of their might.}}}
\VersePair{25:16}{And I will bring upon Ælam the four winds from the four corners of heaven, and I will disperse them toward all these winds; and there shall be no nation to which they shall not come— even the outcasts of Ælam.}{49:36}{{\raggedright I will bring on Elam the four winds from the four quarters of the sky, \poemline{2}{and will scatter them toward all those winds.}\poemline{2}{There will be no nation where the outcasts of Elam will not come.}}}
\VersePair{25:17}{And I will put them in fear before their enemies that seek their life; and I will bring evils upon them according to my great anger; and I will send forth my sword after them, until I have utterly destroyed them.}{49:37}{{\raggedright I will cause Elam to be dismayed before their enemies, \poemline{2}{and before those who seek their life.}\poemline{1}{I will bring evil on them, even my fierce anger,’ says Yahweh;}\poemline{2}{‘and I will send the sword after them,}\poemline{2}{until I have consumed them.}}}
\VersePair{25:18}{And I will set my throne in Ælam, and will send forth thence king and rulers.}{49:38}{{\raggedright I will set my throne in Elam, \poemline{2}{and will destroy from there king and princes,’ says Yahweh.}}}
\VersePair{25:19}{But it shall come to pass at the end of days, that I will turn the captivity of Ælam, saith the Lord.}{49:39}{{\raggedright ‘But it will happen in the latter days \poemline{2}{that I will reverse the captivity of Elam,’ says Yahweh.”}}}
\VersePair{25:20}{In the beginning of the reign of king Sedekias, there came this word concerning Ælam.}{49:34}{Yahweh’s word that came to Jeremiah the prophet concerning Elam, in the beginning of the reign of Zedekiah king of Judah, saying,}
\end{paracol}
\ChapterHeading{26}
\begin{paracol}{2}
\VersePair{26:2}{For Egypt, against the Power of Pharao Nechao King of Egypt, who was by the river Euphrates in Charmis, whom Nabuchodonosor king of Babylon smote in the fourth year of Joakim king of Juda.}{46:1-46:2}{Yahweh’s word which came to Jeremiah the prophet concerning the nations. Of Egypt: concerning the army of Pharaoh Necoh king of Egypt, which was by the river Euphrates in Carchemish, which Nebuchadnezzar king of Babylon struck in the fourth year of Jehoiakim the son of Josiah, king of Judah.}
\VersePair{26:3}{Take up arms and spears, and draw nigh to battle;}{46:3}{{\raggedright “Prepare the buckler and shield, \poemline{2}{and draw near to battle!}}}
\VersePair{26:4}{and harness the horses: mount, ye horsemen, and stand ready in your helmets; advance the spears, and put on your breast-plates.}{46:4}{{\raggedright Harness the horses, and get up, you horsemen, \poemline{2}{and stand up with your helmets.}\poemline{1}{Polish the spears,}\poemline{2}{put on the coats of mail.}}}
\VersePair{26:5}{Why do they fear, and turn back? even because their mighty men shall be slain: they have utterly fled, and being hemmed in they have not rallied, saith the Lord.}{46:5}{{\raggedright Why have I seen it? \poemline{2}{They are dismayed and are turned backward.}\poemline{1}{Their mighty ones are beaten down,}\poemline{2}{have fled in haste,}\poemline{2}{and don’t look back.}\poemline{1}{Terror is on every side,”}\poemline{2}{says Yahweh.}}}
\VersePair{26:6}{Let not the swift flee, and let not the mighty man escape to the north: the forces at Euphrates are become feeble, and they have fallen.}{46:6}{{\raggedright “Don’t let the swift flee away, \poemline{2}{nor the mighty man escape.}\poemline{1}{In the north by the river Euphrates}\poemline{2}{they have stumbled and fallen.}}}
\VersePair{26:7}{Who is this that shall come up as a river, and as rivers roll their waves?}{46:7}{{\raggedright “Who is this who rises up like the Nile, \poemline{2}{like rivers whose waters surge?}}}
\VersePair{26:8}{The waters of Egypt shall come up like a river: and he said, I will go up, and will cover the earth, and will destroy the dwellers in it.}{46:8}{{\raggedright Egypt rises up like the Nile, \poemline{2}{like rivers whose waters surge.}\poemline{1}{He says, ‘I will rise up. I will cover the earth.}\poemline{2}{I will destroy cities and its inhabitants.’}}}
\VersePair{26:9}{Mount ye the horses, prepare the chariots; go forth, ye warriors of the Ethiopians, and Libyans armed with shields; and mount, ye Lydians, bend the bow.}{46:9}{{\raggedright Go up, you horses! \poemline{2}{Rage, you chariots!}\poemline{1}{Let the mighty men go out:}\poemline{2}{Cush and Put, who handle the shield;}\poemline{2}{and the Ludim, who handle and bend the bow.}}}
\VersePair{26:10}{And that day shall be to the Lord our God a day of vengeance, to take vengeance on his enemies: and the sword of the Lord shall devour, and be glutted, and be drunken with their blood: for the Lord has a sacrifice from the land of the north at the river Euphrates.}{46:10}{{\raggedright For that day is of the Lord, Yahweh of Armies, \poemline{2}{a day of vengeance,}\poemline{2}{that he may avenge himself of his adversaries.}\poemline{1}{The sword will devour and be satiated,}\poemline{2}{and will drink its fill of their blood;}\poemline{2}{for the Lord, Yahweh of Armies, has a sacrifice in the north country by the river Euphrates.}}}
\VersePair{26:11}{Go up to Galaad, and take balm for the virgin daughter of Egypt: in vain hast thou multiplied thy medicines; there is no help in thee.}{46:11}{{\raggedright Go up into Gilead, and take balm, virgin daughter of Egypt. \poemline{2}{You use many medicines in vain.}\poemline{2}{There is no healing for you.}}}
\VersePair{26:12}{The nations have heard thy voice, and the land has been filled with thy cry: for the warriors have fainted fighting one against another, and both are fallen together.}{46:12}{{\raggedright The nations have heard of your shame, \poemline{2}{and the earth is full of your cry;}\poemline{2}{for the mighty man has stumbled against the mighty,}\poemline{2}{they both fall together.”}}}
\VersePair{26:13}{The Words which the Lord spoke by Jeremias, concerning the coming of the king of Babylon to smite the land of Egypt.}{46:13}{The word that Yahweh spoke to Jeremiah the prophet, how that Nebuchadnezzar king of Babylon should come and strike the land of Egypt:}
\VersePair{26:14}{Proclaim it at Magdol, and declare it at Memphis: say ye, Stand up, and prepare; for the sword has devoured thy yew-tree.}{46:14}{{\raggedright “Declare in Egypt, \poemline{2}{publish in Migdol,}\poemline{2}{and publish in Memphis and in Tahpanhes;}\poemline{1}{say, ‘Stand up, and prepare,}\poemline{2}{for the sword has devoured around you.’}}}
\VersePair{26:15}{Wherefore has Apis fled from thee? thy choice calf has not remained; for the Lord has utterly weakened him.}{46:15}{{\raggedright Why are your strong ones swept away? \poemline{2}{They didn’t stand, because Yahweh pushed them.}}}
\VersePair{26:16}{And thy multitude has fainted and fallen; and each one said to his neighbour, Let us arise, and return into our country to our people, from the Grecian sword.}{46:16}{{\raggedright He made many to stumble. \poemline{2}{Yes, they fell on one another.}\poemline{1}{They said, ‘Arise! Let’s go again to our own people,}\poemline{2}{and to the land of our birth,}\poemline{2}{from the oppressing sword.’}}}
\VersePair{26:17}{Call ye the name of Pharao Nechao king of Egypt, Saon esbeie moed.}{46:17}{{\raggedright They cried there, ‘Pharaoh king of Egypt is but a noise; \poemline{2}{he has let the appointed time pass by.’}}}
\VersePair{26:18}{As I live, saith the Lord God, he shall come as Itabyrion among the mountains, and as Carmel that is on the sea.}{46:18}{{\raggedright “As I live,” says the King, \poemline{2}{whose name is Yahweh of Armies,}\poemline{1}{“surely like Tabor among the mountains,}\poemline{2}{and like Carmel by the sea,}\poemline{2}{so he will come.}}}
\VersePair{26:19}{O daughter of Egypt dwelling at home, prepare thee stuff for removing: for Memphis shall be utterly desolate, and shall be called Woe, because there are no inhabitants in it.}{46:19}{{\raggedright You daughter who dwells in Egypt, \poemline{2}{furnish yourself to go into captivity;}\poemline{1}{for Memphis will become a desolation,}\poemline{2}{and will be burned up,}\poemline{2}{without inhabitant.}}}
\VersePair{26:20}{Egypt is a fair heifer, but destruction from the north is come upon her.}{46:20}{{\raggedright “Egypt is a very beautiful heifer; \poemline{2}{but destruction out of the north has come.}\poemline{2}{It has come.}}}
\VersePair{26:21}{Also her hired soldiers in the midst of her are as fatted calves fed in her; for they also have turned, and fled with one accord: they stood not, for the day of destruction was come upon them, and the time of their retribution.}{46:21}{{\raggedright Also her hired men in the middle of her are like calves of the stall, \poemline{2}{for they also are turned back.}\poemline{2}{They have fled away together.}\poemline{1}{They didn’t stand,}\poemline{2}{for the day of their calamity has come on them,}\poemline{2}{the time of their visitation.}}}
\VersePair{26:22}{Their voice is as that of a hissing serpent, for they go upon the sand; they shall come upon Egypt with axes, as men that cut wood.}{46:22}{{\raggedright Its sound will go like the serpent, \poemline{2}{for they will march with an army,}\poemline{2}{and come against her with axes, as wood cutters.}}}
\VersePair{26:23}{They shall cut down her forest, saith the Lord, for their number cannot at all be conjectured, for it exceeds the locust in multitude, and they are innumerable.}{46:23}{{\raggedright They will cut down her forest,” says Yahweh, \poemline{2}{“though it can’t be searched;}\poemline{1}{because they are more than the locusts,}\poemline{2}{and are innumerable.}}}
\VersePair{26:24}{The daughter of Egypt is confounded; she is delivered into the hands of a people from the north.}{46:24}{{\raggedright The daughter of Egypt will be disappointed; \poemline{2}{she will be delivered into the hand of the people of the north.”}}}
\VersePair{26:25}{Behold, I will avenge Ammon her son upon Pharao, and upon them that trust in him.}{46:25}{Yahweh of Armies, the God of Israel, says: “Behold, I will punish Amon of No, and Pharaoh, and Egypt, with her gods and her kings, even Pharaoh, and those who trust in him.}
\VersePair{26:27}{But fear not thou, my servant Jacob, neither be thou alarmed, Israel: for, behold, I will save thee from afar, and thy seed from their captivity; and Jacob shall return, and be at ease, and sleep, and there shall be no one to trouble him.}{46:27}{{\raggedright “But don’t you be afraid, Jacob my servant. \poemline{2}{Don’t be dismayed, Israel;}\poemline{1}{for, behold, I will save you from afar,}\poemline{2}{and your offspring from the land of their captivity.}\poemline{1}{Jacob will return,}\poemline{2}{and will be quiet and at ease.}\poemline{2}{No one will make him afraid.}}}
\VersePair{26:28}{Fear not thou, my servant Jacob, saith the Lord; for I am with thee: she that was without fear and in luxury, has been delivered up: for I will make a full end of every nation among whom I have thrust thee forth; but I will not cause thee to fail: yet will I chastise thee in the way of judgment, and will not hold thee entirely guiltless.}{46:28}{{\raggedright Don’t be afraid, O Jacob my servant,” says Yahweh, \poemline{2}{“for I am with you;}\poemline{2}{for I will make a full end of all the nations where I have driven you,}\poemline{1}{but I will not make a full end of you,}\poemline{2}{but I will correct you in measure,}\poemline{2}{and will in no way leave you unpunished.”}}}
\end{paracol}
\ChapterHeading{27}
\begin{paracol}{2}
\VersePair{27:1}{The Word of the Lord which He spoke against Babylon.}{50:1}{The word that Yahweh spoke concerning Babylon, concerning the land of the Chaldeans, by Jeremiah the prophet.}
\VersePair{27:2}{Proclaim ye among the Gentiles, and cause the tidings to be heard, and suppress them not: say ye, Babylon is taken, Belus is confounded; the fearless, the luxurious Mærodach is delivered up.}{50:2}{{\raggedright “Declare among the nations and publish, \poemline{2}{and set up a standard;}\poemline{2}{publish, and don’t conceal;}\poemline{1}{say, ‘Babylon has been taken,}\poemline{2}{Bel is disappointed,}\poemline{2}{Merodach is dismayed!}\poemline{1}{Her images are disappointed.}\poemline{2}{Her idols are dismayed.’}}}
\VersePair{27:3}{For a nation has come up against her from the north, he shall utterly ravage her land, and there shall be none to dwell in it, neither man nor beast.}{50:3}{{\raggedright For a nation comes up out of the north against her, \poemline{2}{which will make her land desolate,}\poemline{2}{and no one will dwell in it.}\poemline{1}{They have fled.}\poemline{2}{They are gone,}\poemline{2}{both man and animal.}}}
\VersePair{27:4}{In those days, and at that time, the children of Israel shall come, they and the children of Juda together; they shall proceed, weeping as they go, seeking the Lord their God.}{50:4}{{\raggedright “In those days, and in that time,” says Yahweh, \poemline{2}{“the children of Israel will come,}\poemline{2}{they and the children of Judah together;}\poemline{1}{they will go on their way weeping,}\poemline{2}{and will seek Yahweh their God.}}}
\VersePair{27:5}{They shall ask the way till they come to Sion, for that way shall they set their face; and they shall come and flee for refuge to the Lord their God; for the everlasting covenant shall not be forgotten.}{50:5}{{\raggedright They will inquire concerning Zion with their faces turned toward it, \poemline{2}{saying, ‘Come, and join yourselves to Yahweh in an everlasting covenant}\poemline{2}{that will not be forgotten.’}}}
\VersePair{27:6}{My people have been lost sheep: their shepherds thrust them out, they caused them to wander on the mountains: they went from mountain to hill, they forgot their resting-place.}{50:6}{{\raggedright My people have been lost sheep. \poemline{2}{Their shepherds have caused them to go astray.}\poemline{1}{They have turned them away on the mountains.}\poemline{2}{They have gone from mountain to hill.}\poemline{2}{They have forgotten their resting place.}}}
\VersePair{27:7}{All that found them consumed them: their enemies said, Let us not leave them alone, because they have sinned against the Lord: he that gathered their fathers had a pasture of righteousness.}{50:7}{{\raggedright All who found them have devoured them. \poemline{2}{Their adversaries said, ‘We are not guilty,}\poemline{1}{because they have sinned against Yahweh,}\poemline{2}{the habitation of righteousness,}\poemline{2}{even Yahweh, the hope of their fathers.’}}}
\VersePair{27:8}{Flee ye out of the midst of Babylon, and from the land of the Chaldeans, and go forth, and be as serpents before sleep.}{50:8}{{\raggedright “Flee out of the middle of Babylon! \poemline{2}{Go out of the land of the Chaldeans,}\poemline{2}{and be as the male goats before the flocks.}}}
\VersePair{27:9}{For, behold, I stir up against Babylon the gatherings of nations out of the land of the north; and they shall set themselves in array against her: thence shall she be taken, as the dart of an expert warrior shall not return empty.}{50:9}{{\raggedright For, behold, I will stir up \poemline{2}{and cause to come up against Babylon a company of great nations from the north country;}\poemline{2}{and they will set themselves in array against her.}\poemline{1}{She will be taken from there.}\poemline{2}{Their arrows will be as of an expert mighty man.}\poemline{2}{None of them will return in vain.}}}
\VersePair{27:10}{And Chaldea shall be a spoil: all that spoil her shall be satisfied.}{50:10}{{\raggedright Chaldea will be a prey. \poemline{2}{All who prey on her will be satisfied,” says Yahweh.}}}
\VersePair{27:11}{Because ye rejoiced, and boasted, while plundering mine heritage; because ye exulted as calves in the grass, and pushed with the horn as bulls.}{50:11}{{\raggedright “Because you are glad, \poemline{2}{because you rejoice,}\poemline{1}{O you who plunder my heritage,}\poemline{2}{because you are wanton as a heifer that treads out the grain,}\poemline{2}{and neigh as strong horses,}}}
\VersePair{27:12}{Your mother is greatly ashamed; your mother that bore you for prosperity is confounded: she is the last of the nations, desolate,}{50:12}{{\raggedright your mother will be utterly disappointed. \poemline{2}{She who bore you will be confounded.}\poemline{1}{Behold, she will be the least of the nations,}\poemline{2}{a wilderness, a dry land, and a desert.}}}
\VersePair{27:13}{by reason of the Lord's anger: it shall not be inhabited, but it shall be all a desolation; and every one that passes through Babylon shall scowl, and they shall hiss at all her plague.}{50:13}{{\raggedright Because of Yahweh’s wrath she won’t be inhabited, \poemline{2}{but she will be wholly desolate.}\poemline{1}{Everyone who goes by Babylon will be astonished,}\poemline{2}{and hiss at all her plagues.}}}
\VersePair{27:14}{Set yourselves in array against Babylon round about, all ye that bend the bow; shoot at her, spare not your arrows,}{50:14}{{\raggedright Set yourselves in array against Babylon all around, \poemline{2}{all you who bend the bow;}\poemline{2}{shoot at her.}\poemline{1}{Spare no arrows,}\poemline{2}{for she has sinned against Yahweh.}}}
\VersePair{27:15}{and prevail against her: her hands are weakened, her bulwarks are fallen, and her wall is broken down: for it is vengeance from God: take vengeance upon her; as she has done, do to her.}{50:15}{{\raggedright Shout against her all around. \poemline{2}{She has submitted herself.}\poemline{2}{Her bulwarks have fallen.}\poemline{1}{Her walls have been thrown down,}\poemline{2}{for it is the vengeance of Yahweh.}\poemline{1}{Take vengeance on her.}\poemline{2}{As she has done, do to her.}}}
\VersePair{27:16}{Utterly destroy seed out of Babylon, and him that holds a sickle in time of harvest: for fear of the Grecian sword, they shall return every one to his people, and every one shall flee to his own land.}{50:16}{{\raggedright Cut off the sower from Babylon, \poemline{2}{and him who handles the sickle in the time of harvest.}\poemline{1}{For fear of the oppressing sword,}\poemline{2}{they will each return to their own people,}\poemline{2}{and they will each flee to their own land.}}}
\VersePair{27:17}{Israel is a wandering sheep; the lions have driven him out: the king of Assyria first devoured him, and afterward this king of Babylon has gnawed his bones.}{50:17}{{\raggedright “Israel is a hunted sheep. \poemline{2}{The lions have driven him away.}\poemline{1}{First, the king of Assyria devoured him,}\poemline{2}{and now at last Nebuchadnezzar king of Babylon has broken his bones.”}}}
\VersePair{27:18}{Therefore thus saith the Lord; Behold, I will take vengeance on the king of Babylon, and upon his land, as I took vengeance on the king of Assyria.}{50:18}{{\raggedright Therefore Yahweh of Armies, the God of Israel, says: \poemline{1}{“Behold, I will punish the king of Babylon and his land,}\poemline{2}{as I have punished the king of Assyria.}}}
\VersePair{27:19}{And I will restore Israel to his pasture, and he shall feed on Carmel and on mount Ephraim and in Galaad, and his soul shall be satisfied.}{50:19}{{\raggedright I will bring Israel again to his pasture, \poemline{2}{and he will feed on Carmel and Bashan.}\poemline{2}{His soul will be satisfied on the hills of Ephraim and in Gilead.}}}
\VersePair{27:20}{In those days, and at that time, they shall seek for the iniquity of Israel, and there shall be none; and for the sins of Juda, and they shall not be found: for I will be merciful to them that are left}{50:20}{{\raggedright In those days, and in that time,” says Yahweh, \poemline{2}{“the iniquity of Israel will be sought for,}\poemline{2}{and there will be none,}\poemline{1}{also the sins of Judah,}\poemline{2}{and they won’t be found;}\poemline{2}{for I will pardon them whom I leave as a remnant.}}}
\VersePair{27:21}{on the land, saith the Lord. Go up against it roughly, and against them that dwell on it: avenge, O sword, and destroy utterly, saith the Lord, and do according to all that I command thee.}{50:21}{{\raggedright “Go up against the land of Merathaim, \poemline{2}{even against it, and against the inhabitants of Pekod.}\poemline{1}{Kill and utterly destroy after them,” says Yahweh,}\poemline{2}{“and do according to all that I have commanded you.}}}
\VersePair{27:22}{A sound of war, and great destruction in the land of the Chaldeans!}{50:22}{{\raggedright A sound of battle is in the land, \poemline{2}{and of great destruction.}}}
\VersePair{27:23}{How is the hammer of the whole earth broken and crushed! How is Babylon become a desolation among the nations!}{50:23}{{\raggedright How the hammer of the whole earth is cut apart and broken! \poemline{2}{How Babylon has become a desolation among the nations!}}}
\VersePair{27:24}{They shall come upon thee, and thou shalt not know it, Babylon, that thou wilt even be taken captive: thou art found and taken, because thou didst resist the Lord.}{50:24}{{\raggedright I have laid a snare for you, \poemline{2}{and you are also taken, Babylon,}\poemline{2}{and you weren’t aware.}\poemline{1}{You are found,}\poemline{2}{and also caught,}\poemline{2}{because you have fought against Yahweh.}}}
\VersePair{27:25}{The Lord has opened his treasury, and brought forth the weapons of his anger: for the Lord God has a work in the land of the Chaldeans.}{50:25}{{\raggedright Yahweh has opened his armory, \poemline{2}{and has brought out the weapons of his indignation;}\poemline{2}{for the Lord, Yahweh of Armies, has a work to do in the land of the Chaldeans.}}}
\VersePair{27:26}{For her times are come: open ye her storehouses: search her as a cave, and utterly destroy her: let there be no remnant of her.}{50:26}{{\raggedright Come against her from the farthest border. \poemline{2}{Open her storehouses.}\poemline{2}{Cast her up as heaps.}\poemline{1}{Destroy her utterly.}\poemline{2}{Let nothing of her be left.}}}
\VersePair{27:27}{Dry ye up all her fruits, and let them go down to the slaughter: woe to them! for their day is come, and the time of their retribution.}{50:27}{{\raggedright Kill all her bulls. \poemline{2}{Let them go down to the slaughter.}\poemline{1}{Woe to them! For their day has come,}\poemline{2}{the time of their visitation.}}}
\VersePair{27:28}{A voice of men fleeing and escaping from the land of Babylon, to declare to Sion the vengeance that comes from the Lord our God.}{50:28}{{\raggedright Listen to those who flee and escape out of the land of Babylon, \poemline{2}{to declare in Zion the vengeance of Yahweh our God,}\poemline{2}{the vengeance of his temple.}}}
\VersePair{27:29}{Summon many against Babylon, even every one that bends the bow: camp against her round about; let no one of her people escape: render to her according to her works; according to all that she has done, do to her: for she has resisted the Lord, the Holy God of Israel.}{50:29}{{\raggedright “Call together the archers against Babylon, \poemline{2}{all those who bend the bow.}\poemline{1}{Encamp against her all around.}\poemline{2}{Let none of it escape.}\poemline{1}{Pay her back according to her work.}\poemline{2}{According to all that she has done, do to her;}\poemline{1}{for she has been proud against Yahweh,}\poemline{2}{against the Holy One of Israel.}}}
\VersePair{27:30}{Therefore shall her young men fall in the streets, and all her warriors shall be cast down, saith the Lord.}{50:30}{{\raggedright Therefore her young men will fall in her streets. \poemline{2}{All her men of war will be brought to silence in that day,” says Yahweh.}}}
\VersePair{27:31}{Behold, I am against thee the haughty one, saith the Lord: for thy day is come, and the time of thy retribution.}{50:31}{{\raggedright “Behold, I am against you, you proud one,” says the Lord, Yahweh of Armies; \poemline{2}{“for your day has come,}\poemline{2}{the time that I will visit you.}}}
\VersePair{27:32}{And thy pride shall fail, and fall, and there shall be no one to set it up again: and I will kindle a fire in her forest, and it shall devour all things round about her.}{50:32}{{\raggedright The proud one will stumble and fall, \poemline{2}{and no one will raise him up.}\poemline{1}{I will kindle a fire in his cities,}\poemline{2}{and it will devour all who are around him.”}}}
\VersePair{27:33}{Thus saith the Lord; The children of Israel and the children of Juda have been oppressed: all they that have taken them captive have oppressed them together; for they would not let them go.}{50:33}{{\raggedright Yahweh of Armies says: “The children of Israel and the children of Judah are oppressed together. \poemline{2}{All who took them captive hold them fast.}\poemline{2}{They refuse to let them go.}}}
\VersePair{27:34}{But their Redeemer is strong; the Lord Almighty is his name: he will enter into judgment with his adversaries, that he may destroy the earth;}{50:34}{{\raggedright Their Redeemer is strong. \poemline{2}{Yahweh of Armies is his name.}\poemline{1}{He will thoroughly plead their cause,}\poemline{2}{that he may give rest to the earth,}\poemline{2}{and disquiet the inhabitants of Babylon.}}}
\VersePair{27:35}{and he will sharpen a sword against the Chaldeans, and against the inhabitants of Babylon, and upon her nobles and upon her wise men;}{50:35}{{\raggedright “A sword is on the Chaldeans,” says Yahweh, \poemline{2}{“and on the inhabitants of Babylon,}\poemline{2}{on her princes,}\poemline{2}{and on her wise men.}}}
\VersePair{27:36}{a sword upon her warriors, and they shall be weakened: a sword upon their horses, and upon their chariots:}{50:36}{{\raggedright A sword is on the boasters, \poemline{2}{and they will become fools.}\poemline{1}{A sword is on her mighty men,}\poemline{2}{and they will be dismayed.}}}
\VersePair{27:37}{a sword upon their warriors, and upon the mixed people in the midst of her; and they shall be as women: a sword upon the treasures, and they shall be scattered upon her water,}{50:37}{{\raggedright A sword is on their horses, \poemline{2}{on their chariots,}\poemline{2}{and on all the mixed people who are in the middle of her;}\poemline{2}{and they will become as women.}\poemline{1}{A sword is on her treasures,}\poemline{2}{and they will be robbed.}}}
\VersePair{27:38}{and they shall be ashamed: for it is a land of graven images; and in the islands, where they boasted.}{50:38}{{\raggedright A drought is on her waters, \poemline{2}{and they will be dried up;}\poemline{1}{for it is a land of engraved images,}\poemline{2}{and they are mad over idols.}}}
\VersePair{27:39}{Therefore shall idols dwell in the islands, and the young of monsters shall dwell in it: it shall not be inhabited any more for ever.}{50:39}{{\raggedright Therefore the wild animals of the desert \poemline{2}{with the wolves will dwell there.}\poemline{1}{The ostriches will dwell therein.}\poemline{2}{It will be inhabited no more forever,}\poemline{2}{neither will it be lived in from generation to generation.}}}
